<script>
	function goToTopic(topic) {
		var topicMap = applySpecialCharacterMapping(topic); 
		var url = "/xpl/topicbrowse.jsp?topic=" + escape(topicMap);
		window.top.location.href = url;
	}
</script>

		<!-- ngIf: vm.loading -->
		<!-- ngIf: !vm.loading --><div ng-if="!vm.loading" class="ng-scope">

	<div class="pure-g">
		<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage --><div ng-if="::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage" ng-class="vm.details.graphicalAbstract ? 'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1' : 'pure-u-1-1'" class="ng-scope pure-u-1-1">
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement -->
		<!--/div-->
		<!--div ng-class="{'pure-u-14-24 u-pr-1':  vm.details.graphicalAbstract, 'pure-u-1-1': ! vm.details.graphicalAbstract}"-->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract --><div ng-if="::vm.details.abstract" class="ng-scope">
				<strong>Abstract:</strong>
				<div class="abstract-text ng-binding" ng-bind-html="::vm.details.abstract">This paper presents a new design for a CMOS double-sideband (DSB) RF transmitter (TX) integrated circuit (IC) for UHF RF indentification (RFID) reader system-on-chip. Due to the strong demand for high linearity, low TX noise, and low cost, a CMOS passive up-conversion mixer with an adaptive bias circuit is proposed. High linearity of the passive mixer can be maintained over a wide range of dc levels from the dc-coupled IF signals using the proposed adaptive biasing circuit. A linear two-stage CMOS power amplifier (PA) follows the up-conversion mixer so that the overall third-order output intercept point (OIP3) of the two-stage PA is improved by the optimized design of the first stage in its biasing condition, the cell size, and due to inter-stage matching. The designed TX IC is fabricated using a 0.18-μm standard CMOS process and the implemented passive mixer exhibits a low double-sideband noise figure (DSB NF) of 4 dB and a high OIP3 of 13.3 dBm. The implemented PA exhibits a high-output 1-dB compression point (OP1dB) of 18 dBm, and a clear sweet spot in OIP3 of as high as 36.8 dBm at the two-tone average output power of 10 dBm. The implemented overall TX IC has a size of 960 × 670 × μm<sup>2</sup> and the overall circuit performed with a gain of 17.8 dB, a high OP1dB of 17.6 dBm, an OIP3 of 28 dBm, and has a low DSB NF of 11.2 dB while consuming a biasing current of 58 mA from a 3.3-V supply. The proposed design also satisfies the spectral mask of the RFID standard for an output power of up to 18 dBm for the double-sideband amplitude shift-keying signals.</div>
			</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.abstract -->			
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.scope -->
			<!-- ngIf: ::vm.details.purpose -->
		</div><!-- end ngIf: ::vm.details.impactStatement || vm.details.abstract || vm.details.scope || vm.details.purpose  || vm.details.previewImage -->

<div id="BodyWrapper" class="ArticlePage" xmlns:ieee="http://www.ieeexplore.ieee.org"><div id="article">
<div class="section" id="sec1"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION I.</div><h2>Introduction</h2></div><p>RF identification (RFID) is a remote auto-identification technology with a recognition range spanning from a few millimeters to several meters, according to the operational frequency bands and technologies. Due to its advantages, such as fast speed, anticollision characteristics for many tags, improved security, and a relatively long recognition range, the RFID systems technology is expected to replace barcode systems in the near future <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>. In addition, due to its high flexibility and programmability, the RFID technology is continually expanding its application base to various areas such as medical fields, construction, security, transportation, and military usage, as well as logistics. In particular, the UHF band has been highlighted for RFID applications because it allows the system to have relatively long recognition ranges and high data rates <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref1" id="context_ref_1_1">[1]</a>.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a> shows an operational diagram of general UHF band passive RFID systems which differs from other wireless communication systems in that the RFID reader receives backscattered data from the tag while it sends a continuous wave (CW) signal to the tag. Due to the imperfect isolation between the transmitter (TX) and receiver (RX) of the reader, the TX signal, including noise, leaks into the RX path, which can limit the RX sensitivity. When the reader downloads the data to the tag, it has to transmit a modulated signal with low distortion so the TX is required to have very low noise, as well as high linearity characteristics.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig1"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-1-small.gif" alt="Figure 1" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 1. </b><fig><p>Communication between the reader and tags for UHF RFID systems.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>To achieve both low noise and high linearity simultaneously with low cost, the TX circuit in this paper adopts a CMOS passive up-conversion mixer (or the up-mixer) <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref2" id="context_ref_2_1">[2]</a>–<a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref3" id="context_ref_3_1">[3]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref4" id="context_ref_4_1">[4]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref5" id="context_ref_5_1">[5]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref6" id="context_ref_6_1">[6]</a><a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref7" id="context_ref_7_1">[7]</a>. The proposed double-balanced CMOS passive mixer has four switching transistors of which the gates are required to be biased with a proper dc voltage in order to achieve high linearity. The IF input ports (sources) of the switching transistors obtain a baseband signal coupled with a proper dc voltage, which comes from the baseband filter.</p><p>The gate biases of the switching transistors and the dc-coupled IF signals determine the biasing level of the switching transistors, which is very critical to the linearity characteristics of the mixer. However, there can be some variance in the biasing condition of the switching transistors due to different dc offsets or other process variations. From this point of view, this paper suggests an adaptive biasing circuit, which supplies an adaptive dc voltage to bias the gates of the switching transistors, according to the dc level of the IF ports, i.e., the source voltage of the switching transistors.</p><p>The TX circuit also adopts a two-stage balanced power amplifier (PA) whose linearity is improved using the first-stage amplifier as a predistorter of the second-stage amplifier. The third-order intermodulation distortion (IMD3) components, generated by the second-stage amplifier, can be cancelled using the IMD3 components generated by the first-stage amplifier. The bias current, cell size, and load matching network of the first-stage amplifier have all been optimized to achieve the best cancellation conditions. The designed TX IC for the UHF RFID reader, including a double-balanced passive mixer and a two-stage PA, has been fabricated using a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-1-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-1" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.55em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-2"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-3"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-4"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-5"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-6"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-7" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.18-</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-8" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-9"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-10"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-11"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-12"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-13" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-1">{\hbox{0.18-}}\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> standard CMOS process and the up-mixer and PA have been individually evaluated using two-tone signals. In addition, the overall performances of the TX IC have been verified using the double-sideband amplitude shift keying (DSB-ASK) signal from one of the representative modulation standards for UHF RFID <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_1">[8]</a>.</p></div>
<div class="section" id="sec2"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION II.</div><h2>TX Leakage and Its Effect on RX Sensitivity</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2a"><h3>A. TX Leakage</h3><p>A UHF RFID system uses a passive tag, which has no battery, so that it can be permanently in use, and manufactured at low cost. As shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig1" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 1</a>, there are three phases for the communication between the reader and the tag. In the first phase, the reader transmits a carrier signal, which is a CW, to activate and initiate the tag. After activating the tag, the reader starts to send the modulated signal to the tag for query as the second phase. For the third phase, the tag's response is backscattered to the reader, while the reader continues to transmit a CW signal to the tag in order to supply energy for the tagging operation <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref8" id="context_ref_8_2a">[8]</a>. The second and third phases can be repeated to complete the overall communication.</p><p>When the reader receives the tag's response, a significant amount of the TX signal, including TX noise, can leak into the RX path due to imperfect isolation of the isolator and the signal reflections from the antenna, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig2" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 2</a>. Therefore, it is important for the TX of the reader to have low noise characteristics because the leaked TX noise can degrade the RX sensitivity <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref9" id="context_ref_9_2a">[9]</a>, <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref10" id="context_ref_10_2a">[10]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig2"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-2-small.gif" alt="Figure 2" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 2. </b><fig><p>TX and front-end configuration of the RFID reader.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec2b"><h3>B. If the RX bandwidth <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-8-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-107" role="math" style="width: 1.745em; top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-113"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-114"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.526em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1001.38em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-115"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-116"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-117" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">N</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-118" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">F</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 1.384em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-119"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-120"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-121" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-255" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">X</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.28em 2.526em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-257"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-258"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-259"></span></span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-260"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.285em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.6em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-261" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">Γ</span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.841em; left: 0.604em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-262"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-263"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-264" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">A</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-265" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">N</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-266" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">T</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.263em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.07em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-15">{}\Gamma_{\rm ANT}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the antenna reflection coefficient. The equivalent input-referred noise power can be calculated by summing the input-referred RX noise from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn2" href="#deqn2" class="fulltext-link">(2)</a> and the TX noise leakage from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn3" href="#deqn3" class="fulltext-link">(3)</a>. Therefore, the practical sensitivity can be recalculated as <disp-formula id="deqn4" class="display-formula"><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><div class="MathJax_Display"><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-16-Frame" tabindex="0" style="width: 100%;"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-267" role="math" style="width: 100%; display: inline-block; min-width: 13.757em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; font-size: 111%; min-width: 13.757em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.066em 1009.61em 4.508em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em; width: 100%;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-268"><span class="mtable" id="MathJax-Span-269" style="min-width: 13.757em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 100%; height: 0px; min-width: 13.757em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 9.613em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.958em 1009.61em 0.483em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; left: 50%; margin-left: -4.802em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1009.61em 4.508em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 9.613em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1009.61em 4.508em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 50%; margin-left: -4.802em;"><span class="mtd" id="MathJax-Span-279"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-280"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-281" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">S<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-282" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.303em;">=</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-283" style="padding-left: 0.303em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.006em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-284" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-285"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-286"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-287" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-288" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-289"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-290"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-291" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-292" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-293" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-294" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-295" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-296" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">+</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-297" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1002.04em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-298"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-299"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-300" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">S</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-301" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">N</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-302" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">R</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 2.045em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-303"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-304"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-305" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">min</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; position: absolute; width: 1.264em; height: 0px; clip: rect(-0.898em 1001.2em 0.423em -999.997em); top: 0.003em; right: 0.003em; margin-right: 0.003em;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.126em 1001.2em 4.447em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; right: 0.003em;"><span class="mtd" id="mjx-eqn-${\hbox{(4)}}$"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-271"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-272"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-273"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-274"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-275"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-276"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-277"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-278" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">(4)</span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.337em;"></span></span></nobr></span></div><script type="math/tex; mode=display" id="MathJax-Element-16">S = P_{N,{\rm total}}+{\rm SNR}_{\min} \eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</script></tex-math><span class="formula"><span class="link">View Source</span><img aria-describedby="qtip-0" style="display:inline;" title="Right-click on figure or equation for MathML and additional features." data-hasqtip="0" class="qtooltip moreInfo" alt="Right-click on figure for MathML and additional features." src="/assets/img/icon.support.gif" border="0" height="20" width="24" /><span class="tex tex2jax_ignore" style="display:none;">S = P_{N,{\rm total}}+{\rm SNR}_{\min} \eqno{\hbox{(4)}}</span></span></disp-formula> where <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-17-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-306" role="math" style="width: 3.366em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.006em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.01em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.159em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-307"><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-308"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.006em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.186em 1000.78em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-309" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">P<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.123em;"></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -3.901em; left: 0.664em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-310"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-311"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-312" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">N<span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; height: 1px; width: 0.063em;"></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-313" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">,</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-314"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-315"><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-316" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-317" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">o</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-318" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">t</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-319" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">a</span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-320" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">l</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.165em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.397em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.203em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-17">P_{N,{\rm total}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> is the overall input-referred equivalent noise power.</p><p>Assume that the TX output signal is a CW having an output power of 30 dBm and the antenna reflection level is <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-18-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-321" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-322"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-323" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-324"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-325"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-326"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-327"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-328" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">25 dB</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-18">-{\hbox {25 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, the RX would receive a TX leakage signal having a power of about 5 dBm, assuming an almost ideal isolator. Using the equations from <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn1" href="#deqn1" class="fulltext-link">(1)</a> to <a ref-type="disp-formula" anchor="deqn4" href="#deqn4" class="fulltext-link">(4)</a>, the overall RX sensitivity can be calculated based on various system parameters, including the TX parameters, and <a ref-type="table" anchor="table1" class="fulltext-link">Table I</a> shows the calculated overall RX sensitivities using typical system parameters, as shown at the bottom of the table. As the NF of the up-mixer of the TX varies from 4 to 30 dB, it is found that the RX sensitivity ranges from −75.7 to <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-19-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-329" role="math" style="width: 5.468em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 4.928em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1004.93em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-330"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-331" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-332"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-333"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-334"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-335"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-336" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">62.4 dBm</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-19">-{\hbox{62.4 dBm}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, which is clearly seen to drastically deteriorate from the value without TX noise leakage, and thus the up-mixer should be carefully designed to have better RX sensitivity. In this analysis, a contribution of the phase noise of the local oscillator (LO) signal to the RX sensitivity is not considered because advantage can be taken of the range correlation effect for this specific application <a ref-type="bibr" anchor="ref11" id="context_ref_11_2b">[11]</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table1"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table I </b>RX Sensitivities Calculated in the Presence of TX Noise Leakage<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-1-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-1-small.gif" alt="Table I" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec3"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION III.</div><h2>Circuit Design</h2></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3a"><h3>A. Up-Conversion Mixer</h3><p>For the core of the double-balanced passive mixer, as shown in the schematic diagram of <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(a)</a>, the biasing points of the switching transistors must be near the threshold voltage for achieving high linearities. However, if the dc level at the source varies or the threshold voltage of the transistor is shifted due to the process variation, the biased points of the switching transistors could drift from the optimal conditions if the conventional fixed biasing circuits are used.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig3"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-3-small.gif" alt="Figure 3" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 3. </b><fig><p>Schematic diagrams of the CMOS passive up-conversion mixer. (a) Passive switching stage. (b) Overall up-mixer circuit, including the proposed adaptive biasing circuit and the LO buffer.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig3" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 3(b)</a> shows a schematic diagram of the overall up-mixer, including the adaptive biasing circuit and the LO buffer, which consists of a voltage follower to sense the dc voltage of the IF signal, a transistor diode (Q1) to set up the biased level, and some peripheral circuits.</p><p>If the dc voltage at the IF input signal increases, the voltage across <i>RL</i> also increases. Since the transistor Q1 is well biased using a high-impedance current source, the voltage across Q1 is almost constant. The drain voltage of Q1 tracks the dc voltage of the IF input and is directly supplied to the gates of the switching transistors so that the gate-to-source voltages of the switching transistors remain almost constant. Even if the dc voltage of the IF input decreases, the biasing voltages still remains almost constant in the same way.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig4" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 4</a> presents the simulated third-order intermodulation intercept point (IIP3) results for various dc voltages at the IF input. The IIP3 performances without the adaptive bias circuit are also simulated with fixed gate voltages of the switching transistors, which clearly show that good IIP3 performances are maintained over a wide dc voltage range for the mixer with the adaptive biasing circuit, while they are rapidly degraded without it.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig4"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-4-small.gif" alt="Figure 4" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 4. </b><fig><p>Simulated IIP3 performances with and without the adaptive biasing circuit.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec3b"><h3>B. Pa</h3><p>Since RFID systems use the modulated signals with varying envelopes, the PA should be linear. To have sufficient power gain, a two-stage amplifier has been employed. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig5" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 5</a> shows a schematic diagram of the two-stage amplifier, which has balanced and common-source configurations. The amplifier has biasing circuits, an input matching network, a partial inter-stage matching network, and power transistors on chip.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig5"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-5-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-5-small.gif" alt="Figure 5" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 5. </b><fig><p>Schematic diagram of the two-stage PA.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p>The second-stage amplifier has been biased for class-A condition in order to have highly linear operation. For higher linearity, the first-stage amplifier has been optimized in its biasing condition and circuit configuration. The transistor cell sizes for Q1 and Q2, interstage matching, and biasing point have been optimized to improve the overall linearity characteristics generated by the second-stage amplifier.</p><p>As a result, the first-stage amplifier has been optimized for a class-AB operation in which it has shown good characteristics as a predistorter. The resultant IMD3 performance of the overall two-stage amplifier has been improved from that of the second-stage so that the third-order output intercept point (OIP3) performance has been improved after optimization of the first-stage amplifier. This is verified in <a ref-type="sec" anchor="sec4" class="fulltext-link">Section IV</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig6"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-6-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-6-small.gif" alt="Figure 6" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 6. </b><fig><p>Schematic diagram of the overall TX including the off-chip circuits for the evaluation.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig7"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-7-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-7-small.gif" alt="Figure 7" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 7. </b><fig><p>(a) Chip microphotograph of the implemented TX IC. (b) Test board for the evaluation of the fabricated TX IC.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig8"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-8-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-8-small.gif" alt="Figure 8" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 8. </b><fig><p>Simulated and measured performances of the implemented up-mixer with an LO power of 0 dBm. (a) Conversion gain and output RF power. (b) IMD3 and IIP3 performances, according to the input power.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec4"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION IV.</div><h2>Fabrication and Experimental Results</h2></div><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a> shows the overall schematic diagram of the TX IC with its external test circuits. The TX IC, including the up-mixer and the PA, is fabricated using TSMC's <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-20-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-337" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.55em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-338"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-339"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-340"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-341"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-342"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-343" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.18-</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-344" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-345"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-346"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-347"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-348"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-349" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-20">{\hbox{0.18-}}\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> CMOS process. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(a)</a> shows a chip microphotograph of the fabricated TX IC having a total size of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-21-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-350" role="math" style="width: 6.79em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 6.129em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.204em 1006.13em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-351"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-352"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-353"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-354"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-355"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-356" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">960</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-357" style="font-family: MathJax_Main; padding-left: 0.243em;">×</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-358" style="padding-left: 0.243em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-359"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-360"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-361"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-362" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">670</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-363" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="msubsup" id="MathJax-Span-364"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 1.264em; height: 0px;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(3.426em 1000.84em 4.207em -999.997em); top: -4.021em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-365"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-366"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-367"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-368"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-369" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span><span style="position: absolute; top: -4.381em; left: 0.844em;"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-370"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-371"><span class="mn" id="MathJax-Span-372" style="font-size: 70.7%; font-family: MathJax_Main;">2</span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 4.027em;"></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.27em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-21">{\hbox{960}} \times {\hbox{670}} \mu{\hbox {m}}^{2}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, including the bonding pads. A test board for evaluation of the fabricated TX IC is shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig7" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 7(b)</a>.</p><div class="section_2" id="sec4a"><h3>A. Up-Conversion Mixer</h3><p>The designed up-mixer, consisting of a double-balanced passive mixer core, an adaptive biasing circuit, and an LO buffer, has been evaluated at the UHF band of 900 MHz with an LO power of 0 dBm with a balanced IF input signal, having a frequency of 10 MHz, being applied to it.</p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(a)</a> shows the simulated and measured voltage conversion gains and output powers according to the input power level. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig8" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 8(b)</a> shows the simulated and measured IMD3 and IIP3 performances according to the input power level. The achieved performances are summarized as a voltage conversion gain of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-22-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-373" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.49em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-374"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-375" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-376"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-377"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-378"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-379"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-380" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3.7 dB</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-22">-{\hbox {3.7 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, a high-output 1-dB compression point (OP1dB) of 5.3 dBm, a high IIP3 of 20 dBm, an OIP3 of 13.3 dBm and a double-sideband noise figure (DSB NF) of 4 dB under a biased supply of 3.3 V and a dc current of 9 mA. Most of the dc current is consumed by the LO buffer and there are some discrepancies in the linearity characteristics between the simulated and measured performances, which are mainly caused by the parasitic components of the interconnections and the pads. The performances of the implemented up-mixer, compared to representative previous works, are presented in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table2" class="fulltext-link">Table II</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full table" id="table2"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table II </b>Performance Summary and Comparison for the Implemented Passive Up-Conversion Mixer<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-2-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-2-small.gif" alt="Table II" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig9" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 9</a> shows the measured IIP3 over various input dc levels, which clearly represent the effects of the adaptive biasing circuit to show that the implemented up-mixer has the capability to maintain its highly linear performance through the wide-input dc-voltage range.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig9"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-9-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-9-small.gif" alt="Figure 9" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 9. </b><fig><p>Measured IIP3 performances according to the various input dc voltages.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full" id="fig10"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-10-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-10-small.gif" alt="Figure 10" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 10. </b><fig><p>Measured OIP3 performances of the implemented PA. (a) Fixed current of 10 mA for the first stage. (b) Fixed current of 38 mA for the second stage.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4b"><h3>B. Pa</h3><p>The designed CMOS PA, with common-source, balanced, and two-stage configurations has been evaluated for the UHF RFID band of 900 MHz. To verify the linearity improvements, the biasing currents of both stages have been adjusted using the voltage sources applied to the VREF1 and VREF2 ports, which directly change the biasing currents of the RF transistors for the first and second stages, respectively.</p><p>The measured OIP3 performances, according to the biasing conditions, are shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10</a>, where <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10(a)</a> presents the measured OIP3 performances with a fixed current of the first stage at 10 mA, while sweeping the dc current of the second stage from 34 to 42 mA and <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig10" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 10(b)</a> presents the measured OIP3 performances with a fixed current of the second stage at 38 mA, while sweeping the dc current of the first stage from 2 to 12 mA.</p><p>The optimal biasing points for both stages can be chosen as 38 and 10 mA for the second and first stages, respectively. At the chosen biased conditions, the overall two-stage amplifier shows the best OIP3 performance of 36.8 dBm at an output power of 10 dBm. The optimized CMOS PA also attains a power gain of 24.5 dB and an output power at 1 dB compression point (P1dB) of 17.6 dBm. A required gain step of 4 dB can be achieved by lowering the biasing current of the first stage from 10 to 2 mA without changing the biasing current of the second stage. Even for this low gain mode, the linearity is not degraded significantly. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig11" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 11</a> represents the performances of the implemented CMOS PA at the optimized bias conditions for both the high and low gain modes. <a ref-type="table" anchor="table3" class="fulltext-link">Table III</a> summarizes the measured performances of the implemented PA.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig11"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-11-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-11-small.gif" alt="Figure 11" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 11. </b><fig><p>Performances of the implemented CMOS PA. (a) Gain. (b) IMD3 and OIP3 for the high and low gain modes.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table3"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table III </b>Performance Summary of the Implemented PA<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-3-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-3-small.gif" alt="Table III" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p></div><div class="section_2" id="sec4c"><h3>C. Overall TX</h3><p>The fabricated TX IC has been evaluated for the UHF RFID band of 900 MHz and a proper output matching network and a transformer to make the balanced signal to a single-ended one, are implemented on the test board, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig6" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 6</a>. It is possible to have an operation with two gain modes by adjusting the biasing condition of the first-stage PA. A gain step of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-23-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-381" role="math" style="width: 3.066em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 2.766em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1002.71em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-382"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-383" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-384"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-385"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-386"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-387"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-388" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">4 dB</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-23">-{\hbox {4 dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> from the nominal high gain mode can be achieved by lowering the biasing current of the first-stage PA from 10 to 2 mA. Due to the imperfect interconnection on the CMOS substrate between the up-mixer and the PA itself, the overall performances are a little degraded from those of the PA, but because of the low NF of the up-mixer, the TX leakage noise of the implemented TX IC is expected to be extremely low.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig12"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-12-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-12-small.gif" alt="Figure 12" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 12. </b><fig><p>Measured performances of the implemented TX IC. (a) Gain. (b) IMD3 and OIP3.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div>
<div class="figure figure-full table" id="table4"><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Table IV </b>Performance Comparison with Previous Work<div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></div><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-4-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-table-4-small.gif" alt="Table IV" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div></div><p></p><p>
<a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(a)</a> shows the measured voltage conversion gains for the high and low gain modes, according to the output power for one-tone signals. <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig12" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 12(b)</a> shows the measured IMD3 and OIP3 performances according to the output power for two-tone signals. When applying an LO signal, with a power of 0 dBm, and an IF signal as the input, the following performances are achieved at the high gain mode: a voltage conversion gain of 17.8 dB, an output P1dB of 17.6 dBm, a high OIP3 of 28 dBm, and an extremely low DSB NF of 11.2 dB with a single bias supply of 3.3 V, which consumes an overall dc current of 58 mA. The measured performances, compared to previous works, are summarized in <a ref-type="table" anchor="table4" class="fulltext-link">Table IV</a>.
</p><div class="figure figure-full" id="fig13"><!--          Workaround for combined images.Eg.- 1000116 Fig. 5        --><div class="img-wrap"><a href="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-13-large.gif"><img src="/mediastore/IEEE/content/media/22/5662237/5593903/5593903-fig-13-small.gif" alt="Figure 13" /><div class="zoom" title="View Larger Image"></div></a></div><div class="figcaption"><b class="title">Fig. 13. </b><fig><p>Measured output spectra. (a) Two-tone signal. (b) DSB-ASK modulated signal, at an average output power of 12 and 15 dBm, respectively.</p></fig></div><p class="links"><a href="/document/5593903/all-figures" class="all">View All</a></p></div><p></p><p><a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13(a)</a> shows the measured two-tone output spectra of the TX for an average output power of 12 dBm. A DSB-ASK baseband signal, which is one of the representative modulation standards for UHF RFID systems, has been applied to the implemented TX. For an output power of 15 dBm, as shown in <a ref-type="fig" anchor="fig13" class="fulltext-link">Fig. 13(b)</a>, the output spectra satisfies the RFID spectral mask with sufficient margin.</p></div></div>
<div class="section" id="sec5"><div class="header article-hdr"><div class="kicker">		                        SECTION V.</div><h2>Conclusions</h2></div><p>Since the UHF RFID reader receives a backscattered signal from the tag while it transmits a CW signal, the RX sensitivity depends not only on the RX circuits, but also on the TX circuits. Hence, the TX IC strongly requires both high linearity and low NF. In this paper, a CMOS passive mixer and highly linear PA have been employed to meet these requirements.</p><p>A CMOS double-balanced passive mixer and a highly linear two-stage PA have been designed for the TX of the UHF RFID reader system-on-chip (SoC). The up-mixer has an adaptive biasing circuit to dynamically track the input dc voltage and supply the required proper gate-to-source voltages to the switching transistors. In this way, the proposed adaptive biasing circuit allows the mixer to maintain its highly linear characteristics over a wide range of input dc voltages, coupled with the IF signal. A two-stage balanced CMOS PA has also been designed in which the first stage is optimized to work as a predistorter for the second stage.</p><p>Using a <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-24-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-389" role="math" style="width: 3.967em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.547em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.384em 1003.55em 2.646em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-390"><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-391"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-392"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-393"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-394"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-395" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">0.18-</span></span></span></span></span><span class="mi" id="MathJax-Span-396" style="font-family: MathJax_Math-italic;">μ</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-397"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-398"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-399"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-400"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-401" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">m</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.33em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 1.137em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-24">{\hbox{0.18-}}\mu{\hbox {m}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula> commercial CMOS process, the designed TX IC has been fabricated and evaluated for the UHF band. The implemented up-mixer exhibits good performances, such as having a conversion gain of <inline-formula id=""><tex-math notation="TeX"><span class="MathJax_Preview"></span><span class="MathJax" id="MathJax-Element-25-Frame" tabindex="0"><nobr><span class="math" id="MathJax-Span-402" role="math" style="width: 3.667em; display: inline-block;"><span style="display: inline-block; position: relative; width: 3.306em; height: 0px; font-size: 111%;"><span style="position: absolute; clip: rect(1.324em 1003.25em 2.405em -999.997em); top: -2.219em; left: 0.003em;"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-403"><span class="mo" id="MathJax-Span-404" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">−</span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-405"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-406"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-407"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-408"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-409" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">3.7</span></span></span></span></span><span class="texatom" id="MathJax-Span-410"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-411"><span class="mstyle" id="MathJax-Span-412"><span class="mrow" id="MathJax-Span-413"><span class="mtext" id="MathJax-Span-414" style="font-family: MathJax_Main;">dB</span></span></span></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; width: 0px; height: 2.225em;"></span></span></span><span style="display: inline-block; overflow: hidden; vertical-align: -0.063em; border-left: 0px solid; width: 0px; height: 0.937em;"></span></span></nobr></span><script type="math/tex" id="MathJax-Element-25">-{\hbox{3.7}} {\hbox {dB}}</script></tex-math></inline-formula>, an input P1dB of 9 dBm, an IIP3 of 19 dBm, and a DSB NF of 4 dB. It is shown that these performances are maintained over a wide range of input dc voltages because of the proposed adaptive biasing scheme. For the implemented PA, a power gain of 24.5 dB, an OP1dB of 17.6 dBm, and a high maximum OIP3 of 36.8 dBm at an output power of 10 dBm are achieved.</p><p>The overall TX IC has been evaluated using an LO signal with a frequency of 900 MHz to determine that an OIP3 of 28 dBm and low DSB NF of 11.2 dB can be obtained. Thanks to the low NF of the up-mixer, the TX noise leakage of the designed TX IC is expected to be extremely low. The proposed new system also satisfies a UHF RFID spectral mask at an output power of 15 dBm with sufficient margin for the baseband DSB-ASK signal excitation. The implemented CMOS TX IC can be adopted in the RFID reader SoC for better RX sensitivity with low cost.</p></div>
</div></div>

	<!-- ngIf: vm.contextData.keywords.length --><div class="stats-keywords-container ng-scope" ng-if="vm.contextData.keywords.length">

				<div>

<script>

function getCookie(name) {
	var nameEQ = name + "=";
	var ca = document.cookie.split(';');
	for(var i=0;i &lt; ca.length;i++) {
		var c = ca[i];
		while (c.charAt(0)==' ') c = c.substring(1,c.length);
		if (c.indexOf(nameEQ) == 0) return c.substring(nameEQ.length,c.length);
	}
	return null;
}

j$('document').ready(function(){
	if(getCookie('legacyUserName')!=null)
	{
		if(IBP_WS_ENABLED_FLAG){
		Modal.refreshLegacyAccountTransition('/xpl/mwLegacyAccountTransition.jsp');
		}
	}
});

</script>

Due to the strong demand for high linearity, low TX noise, and low cost, a CMOS passive up-conversion mixer with an adaptive bias circuit is proposed. High linearity of the passive mixer can be maintained over a wide range of dc levels from the dc-coupled IF signals using the proposed adaptive biasing circuit. A linear two-stage CMOS power amplifier (PA) follows the up-conversion mixer so that the overall third-order output intercept point (OIP3) of the two-stage PA is improved by the optimized design of the first stage in its biasing condition, the cell size, and due to inter-stage matching. The designed TX IC is fabricated using a 0.18-&amp;#x03BC;m standard CMOS process and the implemented passive mixer exhibits a low double-sideband noise figure (DSB NF) of 4 dB and a high OIP3 of 13.3 dBm. The implemented PA exhibits a high-output 1-dB compression point (OP1dB) of 18 dBm, and a clear sweet spot in OIP3 of as high as 36.8 dBm at the two-tone average output power of 10 dBm. The implemented overall TX IC has a size of 960 &amp;#x00D7; 670 &amp;#x00D7; &amp;#x03BC;m&lt;sup&gt;2&lt;/sup&gt; and the overall circuit performed with a gain of 17.8 dB, a high OP1dB of 17.6 dBm, an OIP3 of 28 dBm, and has a low DSB NF of 11.2 dB while consuming a biasing current of 58 mA from a 3.3-V supply. The proposed design also satisfies the spectral mask of the RFID standard for an output power of up to 18 dBm for the double-sideband amplitude shift-keying
